<div id="review_2711369201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2711369201" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2711369201?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782110187" href="/book/show/17899631-the-garden-of-evening-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2711369201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14091115731710227695">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br/><br/>There’s no denying that The Garden of Evening Mists is a wonderful piece of literature. The writing is beautiful and tragic at the same time, with hidden meanings buried deep within the characters words. It also manages to peel away the many layers of one woman’s incredibly complicated life in Malaya, and the horrors of war, in an almost cinematic way. It’s atmospheric, with a hint of mystery, and you can feel the level of passion </span>
  <span id="freeText14091115731710227695" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br />There’s no denying that The Garden of Evening Mists is a wonderful piece of literature. The writing is beautiful and tragic at the same time, with hidden meanings buried deep within the characters words. It also manages to peel away the many layers of one woman’s incredibly complicated life in Malaya, and the horrors of war, in an almost cinematic way. It’s atmospheric, with a hint of mystery, and you can feel the level of passion and conviction the author brings to the story. <br /><br />But, and this is a big but, I couldn’t love the story. I tried, but I found too many things that distracted me enough to stop me from falling into the richness of the text. For one, I found the dual story telling, which flits between the past and the present, disrupted my enjoyment and flow of the text. I much prefer linear story telling, as it allows me to enjoy the journey alongside the characters. The writing, although excellent, does also lean towards the over-the-top side of descriptive at times, which added to the distracted nature of the story. I found I was largely unmoved by the various horrors I was reading, which proves to me how little involved I got with the story. <br /><br />I also found the pace incredibly slow. Not a lot happens for the first 25% of the book, and at times I was willing anything, or anyone, to do something. Even when the pace does pick up, it tends to ebb and flow to the point where you spend a lot of time reading descriptions of gardening. <br /><br />Yun Ling is reserved and detached and I found her romance with Aritomo stilted and uncomfortable. I couldn’t warm to either of them, and found them quite one dimensional in terms of their character development throughout the book. Yun Ling comes across as quite cold at times, without an ability to express anything. I understand this is probably a result of her time as a prisoner of war, but it did nothing to endear her to me. I found I didn’t care. The secondary characters are even worse, with little or no backstories to support them, and nothing to distinguish between them. <br /><br />Beautiful writing, but it this needs a more powerful character to bring it to life and make me feel something. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14091115731710227695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1445332841" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445332841" />
    <a title="BrokenTune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune"><img alt="BrokenTune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p2/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445332841?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrokenTune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrokenTune" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune">BrokenTune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer632869441700147733">3.5*<br/><i><br/>He touched the envelope on the table. ‘You mentioned that you worked as a researcher for the War Crimes Tribunal.’<br/>‘I wanted to ensure that those who were responsible were punished. I wanted to see that justice was done.’<br/>‘You think I am a fool? It was not all about justice.’<br/>‘It was the only way that I would be allowed to examine the court documents and official records,’ I said. ‘I was searching for information about my camp. I wanted to find where my sister was buried.’<br/>His eyes narrowed. ‘Yo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText632869441700147733" style="display:none">3.5*<br><i><br>He touched the envelope on the table. ‘You mentioned that you worked as a researcher for the War Crimes Tribunal.’<br>‘I wanted to ensure that those who were responsible were punished. I wanted to see that justice was done.’<br>‘You think I am a fool? It was not all about justice.’<br>‘It was the only way that I would be allowed to examine the court documents and official records,’ I said. ‘I was searching for information about my camp. I wanted to find where my sister was buried.’<br>His eyes narrowed. ‘You didn’t know where your camp was located?’<br>‘We were blindfolded when the Japs – when the Japanese – transported us there. It was somewhere deep in the jungle. That was all we knew.’<br>‘The other survivors from your camp, what happened to them?’ A butterfly trembled over the cannas by the verandah. It finally alighted on a leaf, its wings closing together in prayer.<br>‘There were no other survivors.’<br></i><br>There was something really compelling about The Garden of Evening Mists, but despite what you might expect from the above quotation, it was not the plot. In fact, if the book had solely carried its message on the back of the plot, I would not have enjoyed this at all. On the face of it, the plot seems about the atrocities of war, the destruction of peoples lives by it, as well as the damage that is caused by hatred and the longing for revenge, and how difficult it is to not just survive, but live, having experienced all of this.<br><i><br>‘They couldn’t kill me when we were at war. And they couldn’t kill me when I was in the camp,’ he said finally, his voice subdued. ‘But holding on to my hatred for forty-six years . . . that would have killed me.’<br></i><br>I should say, that the only reason that this would not have worked well for me as a plot because I would constantly wonder about the real life stories that the author may have been inspired by, and then would lose interest in fictional accounts of this if there are biographies that would give a factual account. What can I say, I like historical non-fiction. <br><br>However, as mentioned, there is more to the story - I really enjoyed that the book actually changes with every vignette that is disclosed to the reader. What appeared as fact, what I learned about the story and the characters, changes with every new revelation, so much like the chosen subject of the book:<br><i><br>‘Gardens like Yugiri’s are deceptive. They’re false. Everything here has been thought out and shaped and built. We’re sitting in one of the most artificial places you can find.’<br></i><br>On a related and similar note, the story also gives insight into parts of history that aren't usually the focus on popular novels. I loved this. While the main story is set in post-war Malaysia and the main character reflects back on the time of Malaya during the Japanese occupation, Tan Twan Eng also weaves in facts about the colonial regimes in both Malaya and South Africa, and the struggle of the Boers with the British. It's another aspect, or perspective that is reflected in the novels construct of the Garden - the characters describe historical facts by focusing the reader's attention on the characters' backstory, and it works.<br><i><br>‘Tominaga explained it to me,’ I said. ‘But I’ve only just really understood it now – the effect of seeing the view is much more powerful than if the sea has not been obstructed.’<br></i><br>The Garden of Evening Mists may not be the most in-depth work of historical fiction - much of the story is taken up by gardening and (way too much) discussions about gardening - but it makes up for it with vivid descriptions that transported me back to Tanah Rata and the surrounding Cameron Highlands, an area that I enjoyed exploring a few years ago. And of course, the mention of the local tea meant I needed to read the book with a cup close by. Book, tea, memories. <br><i><br>Before me lies a voyage of a million miles, and memory is the moonlight I will borrow to illuminate my way.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466220451i/19454049._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="Cameron Highlands near Tanah Rata, where the novel is set." class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>Cameron Highlands near Tanah Rata, where the novel is set.</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="632869441700147733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_418432158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/418432158" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418432158?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=booker-prize">booker-prize</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=past-and-present">past-and-present</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2011-release">2011-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418432158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1233889007788799722"><i>The Garden of Evening Mists</i> starts in the late 1980s, as retired judge Teoh Yun Ling returns to Yugiri, a property where she spent a period of her life almost forty years earlier, in Malaya during the Japanese occupation. Told in flashbacks as she looks back on her life, the majority of the book is devoted the events of this time. We learn that Yun Ling was the only survivor of a Japanese POW camp - a fact which, in itself, is a source of mystery, as she seems determined not to reveal how she ma</span>
  <span id="freeText1233889007788799722" style="display:none"><i>The Garden of Evening Mists</i> starts in the late 1980s, as retired judge Teoh Yun Ling returns to Yugiri, a property where she spent a period of her life almost forty years earlier, in Malaya during the Japanese occupation. Told in flashbacks as she looks back on her life, the majority of the book is devoted the events of this time. We learn that Yun Ling was the only survivor of a Japanese POW camp - a fact which, in itself, is a source of mystery, as she seems determined not to reveal how she managed to escape. Staying with Marcus and Emily, a pair of family friends originally from South Africa, she seeks out their neighbour Nakamura Aritomo. Formerly gardener to the Emperor of Japan (a fact which causes much moral conflict for Yun Ling), Aritomo is now living in exile and has created an authentic Japanese garden at Yugiri. Mindful of a promise made to her sister, who died in the camp, Yun Ling persuades Aritomo to tutor her so she can create a memorial garden. The story focuses on the developing relationship between Yun Ling and Aritomo, set against a backdrop of political unrest as communist rebels terrorise the surrounding estates.<br /><br />I've read a few reviews of <i>The Garden of Evening Mists</i> which have criticised it for being dull. I can completely understand why some would think that - it's a slow-moving, descriptive book and although there are some dramatic events, it couldn't really be described as action-packed. However, I found it a very soothing read: thoughtful, reflective and intelligent. The story is a very complex one - even having finished the book, I didn't find it easy to write the summary above. There's lots of strands to the plot, lots of characters, lots of background detail, and it does require concentration, but in my opinion at least, it's worth it.<br /><br />I must admit that I was occasionally frustrated by the way the narrative skirted around things rather than addressing them directly, particularly when it came to the relationships between certain characters. I didn't actually realise for quite some time <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[after Yun Ling and Aritomo kissed that they had actually become romantically involved <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, until a throwaway comment from Yun Ling brought it to my attention. Given the animosity and apprehension between the two at the beginning, I would really have liked to know more about how this relationship developed. I felt the main problem with the book was that it didn't explore details like this fully and often seemed to be dwelling more on external events which could have been left out of the story.<br /><br />Overall, though, I really, really liked <i>The Garden of Evening Mists</i>. It's left a memorable impression on me - the time I spent reading it provided me with a true sense of escape. I have the author's acclaimed debut, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1219949.The_Gift_of_Rain" title="The Gift of Rain by Tan Twan Eng" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gift of Rain</a>, on my wishlist now and I'm looking forward to (hopefully) being transported and calmed once again when I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1233889007788799722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1799350981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799350981" />
    <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens"><img alt="DeB MaRtEnS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593294620p2/9827967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799350981?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781602861800" href="/book/show/13592384-the-garden-of-evening-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=outstanding-bests">outstanding-bests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=africa-mideast-asia">africa-mideast-asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=memorably-good">memorably-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=war-stories">war-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=beloved-by-me">beloved-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=dramatic-fiction">dramatic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=2017-notable">2017-notable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799350981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15971526829292208289">The Garden of the Evening Mists is a "literary novel", with a capital L. It requires concentration. It delivers prose which insists that you stop and read again, look at the words which take you into the stillness of the garden. It forces you to focus, because this narrative moves fluidly in time, between people and love and cruelty and memory. It tells a story of wartime in what is now Malaysia, its aftermath from the occupation of the harsh Japanese and a country devastated by a loss of trust </span>
  <span id="freeText15971526829292208289" style="display:none">The Garden of the Evening Mists is a "literary novel", with a capital L. It requires concentration. It delivers prose which insists that you stop and read again, look at the words which take you into the stillness of the garden. It forces you to focus, because this narrative moves fluidly in time, between people and love and cruelty and memory. It tells a story of wartime in what is now Malaysia, its aftermath from the occupation of the harsh Japanese and a country devastated by a loss of trust in its Colonial British government, a land threatened by murderous guerrilla Communist terrorists and exhausted people. And so much more...<br /><br />During a bit of a former reading vacuum, my inclination was to peruse the innumerable LISTS which categorize books by some notable feature or another. Somehow, I found myself among winners of The Man Asian Literary Prize, many short and longlisted for the Booker, a veritable deep well of literature from Asia and most of which I had been unaware. These were not the stuff of cozy mysteries or #1 bestsellers, well marketed to a huge audience. These had grit... Herein I discovered The Garden of Evening Mists, the book cover inviting me in. <br /><br />The plot is complex. At times I found myself either in the past of 1951 or the present of the novel, confusingly unable to discern where in time Yun Ling Teoh was. At the novel's opening, Yun Ling has retired from her profession as Judge and has returned to Yugiro, in the Cameron Highlands. At sixty-three she continues to bear the scars of the Japanese wartime camp, haunted by her sister's death. <br /><br />Yun Ling is also battling a rare neurological disease, which will claim her ability to understand writing. After a professor visits to view the Japanese woodcuts in Yun's possession, she is prompted to write about Aritomo, the Japanese gardener who also created the garden, who took her as an apprentice in 1951, whose lives had intersections on one another's path- and which she will only discover by reaching back into the stillness of her fading memory, a place she hoped to never revisit. <br /><br />Her memories are moved to appear as she notices the jungle, the light of the sun, an archery bow... the sequence as haphazard as the triggers themselves. Gradually, a picture begins to emerge slowly, pieces of people, conversations fragmented becoming a whole, and Yun Lin sees Aritomo and herself differently. <br /><br />"Before me lies a voyage of a million miles, and memory is the moonlight I will borrow to illuminate my way. <br /> The lotus flowers are opening in the first rays of the sun. Tomorrow's rain lies on the horizon, but high up in the sky something pale and small is descending, growing in size as it falls. I watch the heron circle the pond, a leaf spiraling down to the water, setting off silent ripples across the garden."<br /><br /><br />A beautiful, deliberate and atmospheric novel. Highly recommended for readers wanting a mental stretch. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15971526829292208289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_428538236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428538236" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/428538236?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2012">read2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=booker-winners-and-listed">booker-winners-and-listed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=location-malaysia">location-malaysia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428538236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7864331563381338025">This is a truly incredible book, and is my pick to win the Man Booker Prize this year, and I say that even before reading the last of the six.<br/><br/>Publisher summary: <i>After studying law at Cambridge and time spent helping to prosecute Japanese war criminals, Yun Ling Teoh, herself the scarred lone survivor of a brutal Japanese wartime camp, seeks solace among the jungle-fringed plantations of Northern Malaya where she grew up as a child. There she discovers Yugiri, the only Japanese garden in Malaya, </i></span>
  <span id="freeText7864331563381338025" style="display:none">This is a truly incredible book, and is my pick to win the Man Booker Prize this year, and I say that even before reading the last of the six.<br /><br />Publisher summary: <i>After studying law at Cambridge and time spent helping to prosecute Japanese war criminals, Yun Ling Teoh, herself the scarred lone survivor of a brutal Japanese wartime camp, seeks solace among the jungle-fringed plantations of Northern Malaya where she grew up as a child. There she discovers Yugiri, the only Japanese garden in Malaya, and its owner and creator, the enigmatic Aritomo, exiled former gardener of the Emperor of Japan. Despite her hatred of the Japanese, Yun Ling seeks to engage Aritomo to create a garden in Kuala Lumpur, in memory of her sister who died in the camp.</i><br /><br />The story is told in a dual way with some side trips. Part of the story comes from the time shortly after Yun Ling is no longer a POW, and part of the story comes from the time after she has retired from being a judge and comes back to the garden. She has aphasia and is trying to capture as much of her life as she can before she loses her memory. The author does something really interesting with the storytelling in that she will have a conversation in her present-day life in one chapter where a phrase or person will be mentioned, but as the reader you don't discover the details about the person or phrase until she goes back to tell the story. It isn't done in an obvious way, but in the natural way that stories unfold, where a passing mention of something can recall a memory you didn't even know you have access to anymore. <br /><br />I learned a lot about Malaya/Malaysia from British and Dutch occupation to World War II to the "Malayan Emergency." The philosophy behind Japanese gardening and the Tao Te Ching both weave their way throughout the novel, and the author seems to embrace the aesthetics of both in his writing as well. While Yun Ling is being taught to slow down, breathe, focus; I felt I was being asked to do that as a reader. <br /><br />I can't pick out specific examples because this is a novel that should be experienced as a whole. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7864331563381338025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="elementListBrownSeparator"></div>



  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_454822293" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454822293" />
    <a title="Rusalka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6163718-rusalka"><img alt="Rusalka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591511894p2/6163718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454822293?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rusalka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rusalka" href="/user/show/6163718-rusalka">Rusalka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781905802623" href="/book/show/12031533-the-garden-of-evening-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=ylto-alphabet">ylto-alphabet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=original-52-books-around-the-world">original-52-books-around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=booker">booker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=ylto-topplers">ylto-topplers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454822293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4437700968847950258">I'm going to do something in this post that I have noticed no one else who has done a "proper" review that I have read of this book has done. In fact, two things. By proper I mean reviews that have been published in old school places like literary reviews, and book sections of newspapers. I tend to read a book then have a quick look around the web for other peoples thoughts. Today's scout disappointed me.<br/><br/>So here it is.<br/>1. I am not going to spoil the book. Unlike every review I have read, I am not</span>
  <span id="freeText4437700968847950258" style="display:none">I'm going to do something in this post that I have noticed no one else who has done a "proper" review that I have read of this book has done. In fact, two things. By proper I mean reviews that have been published in old school places like literary reviews, and book sections of newspapers. I tend to read a book then have a quick look around the web for other peoples thoughts. Today's scout disappointed me.<br /><br />So here it is.<br />1. I am not going to spoil the book. Unlike every review I have read, I am not going to give away a plot twist or the end of the book. Seriously. Who thinks that's a good idea?<br />2. I'm going to get my facts right. Most reviews I have read spout all these fact of what happens in the book. I just read it and they are wrong. Did they even bother reading the book? Or just the blurb on the back and some Goodreads or Amazon reviews? Bah.<br /><br />After that build up. I really enjoyed it. REALLY! The book is the story of a Supreme Court judge in Malaysia who retires (first chapter, not a spoiler). She heads up to a house she owns in the Cameron Highlands, and meets up with an old friend who still lives in the area. We then get told the story of her now, mixed with the stories of her past. We learn about the area, her history, the history of the country and about the Garden of Evening Mists.<br /><br />What I loved about this book was the sereneness. The calmness. The stillness. I expected that when we were being walked through a beautiful, sculpted Japanese garden with Taoist, Buddhist and Shinto elements. What I didn't expect was it to trickle out of the garden and into the other elements of the book. Even the more violent or destructive parts of the book. I found that to be quite a skill.<br /><br />I enjoyed the book also as it gave me a peek at the Pacific element of WWII. I am a bit over the European war stories. But this was a part of the war that we were directly a part of in some instances, but we talk very little about. And this was told from the perspective of not only the Malaysian Chinese, but the Japanese as well. Both of these are sides we never hear here in Aus. Then also, the aftermath of the war, with the instability of Malaya before it became Malaysia. I find it astounding we have so many Malays and Malaysian Chinese in Australia, yet we are taught nothing about their history, even the modern stuff. Sometimes I wonder if this is not more relevant than some European history. Mind you, didn't learn a lot of that either.<br /><br />I definitely recommend this as a read. I enjoyed the journey the book took me on. I liked that there was another character in the book that was the garden itself. I am wondering how much gardening advice I can take out of this book to apply to my own overgrown, chaotic garden to instill into it some of the tranquility this book gave me.<br /><br />For more reviews, visit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/">http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4437700968847950258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2707455228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2707455228" />
    <a title="Roman Clodia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia"><img alt="Roman Clodia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464021031p2/56111743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2707455228?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roman Clodia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roman Clodia" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia">Roman Clodia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9781782110194" href="/book/show/18516645-the-garden-of-evening-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2707455228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16509986535391051299">I came to this book ready to love it as so many of my book-friends do... but sadly I found it patchy and episodic. As is so often the case in contemporary novels, it flits between different times: c.1990s (I'm guessing) when the narrator Yun Lin retires from her position as a judge in Malaysia and returns to Majuba where the eponymous garden lies; 1951 when she first becomes the apprentice to a Japanese master-gardener and works with him on Yugiri; and inset stories of her experiences under Japa</span>
  <span id="freeText16509986535391051299" style="display:none">I came to this book ready to love it as so many of my book-friends do... but sadly I found it patchy and episodic. As is so often the case in contemporary novels, it flits between different times: c.1990s (I'm guessing) when the narrator Yun Lin retires from her position as a judge in Malaysia and returns to Majuba where the eponymous garden lies; 1951 when she first becomes the apprentice to a Japanese master-gardener and works with him on Yugiri; and inset stories of her experiences under Japanese occupation during the war. <br /><br />There are also other inset stories such as that of a Japanese professor in the present who was a kamikaze pilot during the war; and the tales of an Afrikaaner family now living in Malaysia who hated the English for their activities during the Boer War. It's hard to see how this all comes together and the lack of organic unity is one of the things that disappointed me.<br /><br />Yun Lin is a hard character to get a handle on: on one hand, she's still known to be bitter about the war, and to hate the Japanese; yet, on the other, she had a Japanese lover in the 1950s. I'd expected the latter story to be more subtle and to interrogate the conflicts between a nation's wartime personality and an individual - but actually this never gets addressed. Yugiri, for sure, is an image of serenity, harmony and beauty in contrast to the atrocities perpetrated by the Japanese army of occupation - but even the garden may have a more sinister purpose...<br /><br />Add to this the boys-own-adventure strand of a missing war-time treasure, and some rather convenient occurences (the kamikaze pilot who's due to fly to his death... but is prevented by the dropping of the atom bomb) and I frequently felt out of kilter with this book. Even the prose style which others have found beautiful felt rather mundane to me: lots of mentions of clouds, mists, herons and stars but no real substance. <br /><br />I was especially disappointed with the clichéd figure of Aritomo: an almost cartoonish amalgamation of 'orientalising' characteristics: he's enigmatic, inscrutable, speaks in Taoist riddles, takes Yun Lin as his disciple, and spends his time creating beauty in his garden, woodblocks and body tattoos - in typical fashion, he disappears mysteriously and leaves just his creations behind. Reparation at the end... or something slightly more sinister? <br /><br />So overall I found this baggy and chaotic - there are powerful sections but they are jumbled up with all kinds of miscellaneous extras. With so much going on, I'd be hard-pressed to say what this is *about*: wasted lives as a result of war? Reparation and recompense through beauty and creation? A potted history of Malaya/Malaysia in the latter half of of the twentieth century? What I will add is that I found this surprisingly emotionally cold.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16509986535391051299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194499045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3016574658614613307">I had an unusual experience with this book: I liked it and appreciated it much more after finishing. While reading it there were sections that struck me with their power or beauty, but I only truly appreciated the author's subtle narrative gifts when looking back. Indeed there were sections I had to slog through, and times I wondered why this or that subplot or chapter was not edited out, but I understood all, once done. <br/><br/>It moves skillfully through gardens and jungle, a Japanese work camp and a </span>
  <span id="freeText3016574658614613307" style="display:none">I had an unusual experience with this book: I liked it and appreciated it much more after finishing. While reading it there were sections that struck me with their power or beauty, but I only truly appreciated the author's subtle narrative gifts when looking back. Indeed there were sections I had to slog through, and times I wondered why this or that subplot or chapter was not edited out, but I understood all, once done. <br /><br />It moves skillfully through gardens and jungle, a Japanese work camp and a tea plantation. It's a humbling book, enigmatic at times, sometimes stark, and lush, and lovely. It defies a quick summary. The complexity of the material, married with the author's beautiful writing, make "The Garden of Evening Mists" unique and worthwhile.</span>

<div id="review_947627123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947627123" />
    <a title="Hana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10571559-hana"><img alt="Hana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458172215p2/10571559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947627123?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hana" href="/user/show/10571559-hana">Hana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781905802623" href="/book/show/12031533-the-garden-of-evening-mists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=far-away-places">far-away-places</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=gardening">gardening</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947627123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14260307519548131970">"The garden has to reach inside you. It should change your heart, sadden it, uplift it. It has to make you appreciate the impermanence of everything in life....that point in time just as the last leaf is about to drop, as the remaining petal is about to fall; that captures everything beautiful and sorrowful about life."<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405107996i/10343011._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the story of a garden and of the man and woman who made the garden. It is a story about remembering, and a story about forgetting. As in all gardens, there is death and de</span>
  <span id="freeText14260307519548131970" style="display:none">"The garden has to reach inside you. It should change your heart, sadden it, uplift it. It has to make you appreciate the impermanence of everything in life....that point in time just as the last leaf is about to drop, as the remaining petal is about to fall; that captures everything beautiful and sorrowful about life."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405107996i/10343011._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the story of a garden and of the man and woman who made the garden. It is a story about remembering, and a story about forgetting. As in all gardens, there is death and decay, but above all there is beauty and, in the end, a sense of moving into a place of perfect stillness and balance.<br><br>The story is set in the highlands of Malaya where "Tea bushes clad the hillsides, shaped into box hedges by decades of picking. Moving between waist-high bushes, workers plucked the leaves with voracious fingers, throwing fistfuls of them over their shoulders into rattan baskets strapped to their backs. The air had a herbal undertone, more a flavor than a scent."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404932324i/10304183._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There, Yun Ling Teo, a survivor of a Japanese prison camp, meets Nakamura Aritomo, once the gardener for the Emperor of Japan. Yun Ling asks Aritomo to create a garden in memory of her sister who died in the camps yet loved the Temple Gardens of Kyoto. Aritomo refuses, but agrees to take Yun Ling as an apprentice so that she can learn to make the garden herself.<br><br>"The girl who had once walked in the gardens of Kyoto with her sister," Aritomo said, peering into my eyes as though searching for a pebble he had dropped into the bottom of a pond, "the girl, is she still there?"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404938428i/10306428.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The earliest gardeners in Japan were monks, recreating the dream of heaven on earth in the monastery grounds.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405109362i/10343251._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"Emptiness: it appealed to me, the possibility of ridding myself of everything I had seen and heard and lived through."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405109555i/10343299._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"This spot where you sit, this is the starting point...this is the place where the first pebble breaks the surface of the water."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405110268i/10343459._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"At each turn in the path, Aritomo drew my attention to an arrangement of rocks, an unusual sculpture, or a stone lantern. They looked as if they had been lying there on the beds of moss and ferns for centuries. 'These objects signal to the traveler that he is entering another layer of his journey,' he said. 'They tell him to stop and gather his thoughts, to savor the view'."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405110360i/10343526._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"The maple...remembered the changing seasons in the expanding circles of its memory: its leaves turned completely red, flaking away from the branches to drift across the garden."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405110567i/10343594._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the end, the garden becomes not a path towards forgetfulness, but instead a form of living memory. "But I won't be able to remember everything," Yun Ling says. Arimoto answers: "The garden will remember it for you."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405110012i/10343387.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was no need to talk much now - we understood each others shades of silence....<br><br>.... A leaf spiraling down to the water, setting off silent ripples across the garden<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1405110744i/10343639._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For two superb, largely spoiler-free reviews see: Scarlett's excellent analysis of the book's contrasting themes: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436722574?book_show_action=true&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> and Jill's beautiful introduction to the story and analysis of the garden as a metaphor: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426358622?book_show_action=true&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br><br>Content rating: PG warning. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Disturbing recollections of Japanese concentration camps, the sufferings of the 'comfort women', tortures, and other war-time horrors. But the sufferings are sketched rather than brutally detailed. Some sex, but all fade to black. Perhaps the strangest element were details surround the making and preserving of whole body tattoos, which I found rather unsettling. But the predominant mood is one of quiet beauty, which somehow managed to soften the hard things. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14260307519548131970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DxSmBy7E9lNew2Tkx3PZMHJeacz8ar/BPQ4Vqv8EkUAil8VG4JMu/2r8v+pnJVZ2jUPGGQ8LxLxVI/DPXhcrsw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i2j1YwYl7uO8TqWLcxNzRCc4YivebB6uFYnis2XbTaOm65YiyHI2T4hxfoXTRfwC2CXN/i0NZdN9pAfWxMj3UA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_239897'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/239897.The_Harmony_Silk_Factory?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Harmony Silk Factory<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/140377.Tash_Aw?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Tash Aw<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.43 avg rating &mdash; 2,219 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2005\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3801437404985891893\">Joseph Conrad, W. Somerset Maugham, and Anthony Burgess have shaped our perceptions of Malaysia. In Tash Aw, we now have an authentic Malaysian voice that remaps this literary landscape.\n\nThe Harmony Silk Factory traces the story of textile merchant <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3801437404985891893\" style=\"display:none\">Joseph Conrad, W. Somerset Maugham, and Anthony Burgess have shaped our perceptions of Malaysia. In Tash Aw, we now have an authentic Malaysian voice that remaps this literary landscape.\n\nThe Harmony Silk Factory traces the story of textile merchant Johnny Lim, a Chinese peasant living in British Malaya in the first half of the twentieth century. Johnny\'s factory is the most impressive structure in the region, and to the inhabitants of the Kinta Valley Johnny is a hero—a Communist who fought the Japanese when they invaded, ready to sacrifice his life for the welfare of his people. But to his son, Jasper, Johnny is a crook and a collaborator who betrayed the very people he pretended to serve, and the Harmony Silk Factory is merely a front for his father\'s illegal businesses. This debut novel from Tash Aw gives us an exquisitely written look into another culture at a moment of crisis.\n\nThe Harmony Silk Factory won the 2005 Whitbread First Novel Award and also made it to Į klestinčią kunigaikščio Boriatinskio sodybą, apsuptą lūžtančio nuo gėrybių sodo. Ir sodyba, ir pats kunigaikščių gyvenimas – kaip šventė: amžina, dosni, džiūgaujanti. Tačiau į šį gyvenimą ateina vėlyvas ir niekieno nelaukiamas vaikas. Dukra, kurios gimimas sugriauna idealiai atrodžiusią šeimą. Tusia nuo gimimo yra kitokia. Patriarchalinėje, tradicijų sukaustytoje visuomenėje, kurioje kiekvienas elgiasi ir gyvena taip, kaip diktuoja luomo taisyklės, ji atrodo, lyg būtų atėjusi iš kito laiko. Ji nuo gimimo daro ką nori, elgiasi kaip neįprastai laisvai, šokiruodama aplinkinius. Ji pati sprendžia, kada jai pradėti kalbėti. Kaip elgtis, kuo domėtis, ką mylėti ir ko neapkęsti – o tai neatleistina toje aplinkoje, kurioje jai tenka gyventi.\n„Sodas“ – knyga, skirta pasiilgusiems klasikinės rusų literatūros. Tai epinis, plačiais mostais nutapytas anuometinės Rusijos paveikslas. Didžiulis Boriatinskių dvaras – tarsi rusiškas pasaulio modelis: su pirkliais ir valstiečiais, prietarais ir pažanga, mergomis patarnautojomis, sėja ir derliaus nuėmimu, sodu, kiaulėmis ir arkliais. Ypač arkliais, kurie Tusiai reiškia daugiau nei žmonės. Visą šį universumą valdo dviese: Nadežda Aleksandrovna Boriatinskaja ir Tusiai ateiti į pasaulį padėjęs vokiečių kilmės daktaras Meizelis.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13847588.Tan_Twan_Eng">About Tan Twan Eng</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13847588.Tan_Twan_Eng"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1500524463p3/13847588.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13080710304765518525">Tan Twan Eng was born in Penang and lived in various places in Malaysia as a child. He studied law at the University of London and later worked as lawyer in one of Kuala Lumpur’s most reputable law firms; in 2016, he was an International Writer-in-Residence at Nanyang Technological University in Singapore. Tan's first novel, <em>The Gift of Rain</em> (2007), was longlisted for the Man Booker Prize and has </span>
  <span id="freeText13080710304765518525" style="display:none">Tan Twan Eng was born in Penang and lived in various places in Malaysia as a child. He studied law at the University of London and later worked as lawyer in one of Kuala Lumpur’s most reputable law firms; in 2016, he was an International Writer-in-Residence at Nanyang Technological University in Singapore. Tan's first novel, <em>The Gift of Rain</em> (2007), was longlisted for the Man Booker Prize and has been translated into Italian, Spanish, Greek, Romanian, Czech and Serbian. <em>The Garden of Evening Mists</em> (2011), his second novel, won the Man Asian Literary Prize and Walter Scott Prize, and was shortlisted for the Man Booker Prize and the International IMPAC Dublin Literary Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13080710304765518525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
